   62: =head1 NAME
   63: 
   64: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor - Extract test schemas from Perl modules
   65: 
   66: =head1 VERSION
   67: 
   68: Version 0.38
   69: 
   70: =cut
   71: 
   72: our $VERSION = '0.38';
   73: 
   74: =head1 SYNOPSIS
   75: 
   76: 	use App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor;
   77: 
   78: 	my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
   79: 		input_file => 'lib/MyModule.pm',
   80: 		output_dir => 'schemas/',
   81: 		verbose	=> 1,
   82: 	);
   83: 
   84: 	my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
   85: 
   86: =head1 DESCRIPTION
   87: 
   88: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor analyzes Perl modules and generates
   89: structured YAML schema files suitable for automated test generation by L<App::Test::Generator>.
   90: This module employs
   91: static analysis techniques to infer parameter types, constraints, and
   92: method behaviors directly from your source code.
   93: 
   94: =head2 Analysis Methods
   95: 
   96: The extractor combines multiple analysis approaches for a comprehensive schema generation:
   97: 
   98: =over 4
   99: 
  100: =item * B<POD Documentation Analysis>
  101: 
  102: Parses embedded documentation to extract:
  103:   - Parameter names, types, and descriptions from =head2 sections
  104:   - Method signatures with positional parameters
  105:   - Return value specifications from "Returns:" sections
  106:   - Constraints (ranges, patterns, required/optional status)
  107:   - Semantic type detection (email, URL, filename)
  108: 
  109: =item * B<Code Pattern Detection>
  110: 
  111: Analyzes source code using PPI to identify:
  112:   - Method signatures and parameter extraction patterns
  113:   - Type validation (ref(), isa(), blessed())
  114:   - Constraint patterns (length checks, numeric comparisons, regex matches)
  115:   - Return statement analysis and value type inference
  116:   - Object instantiation requirements and accessor methods
  117: 
  118: =item * B<Signature Analysis>
  119: 
  120: Examines method declarations for:
  121:   - Parameter names and positional information
  122:   - Instance vs. class method detection
  123:   - Method modifiers (Moose-style before/after/around)
  124:   - Various parameter declaration styles (shift, @_ assignment)
  125: 
  126: =item * B<Heuristic Inference>
  127: 
  128: Applies Perl-specific domain knowledge:
  129:   - Boolean return detection from method names (is_*, has_*, can_*)
  130:   - Common Perl idioms and coding patterns
  131:   - Context awareness (scalar vs list, wantarray usage)
  132:   - Object-oriented patterns (constructors, accessors, chaining)
  133: 
  134: =back
  135: 
  136: =head2 Generated Schema Structure
  137: 
  138: The extracted schemas follow this YAML structure:
  139: 
  140:     function: method_name
  141:     module: Package::Name
  142:     input:
  143:       param1:
  144:         type: string
  145:         min: 3
  146:         max: 50
  147:         optional: 0
  148:         position: 0
  149:       param2:
  150:         type: integer
  151:         min: 0
  152:         max: 100
  153:         optional: 1
  154:         position: 1
  155:     output:
  156:       type: boolean
  157:       value: 1
  158:     new: Package::Name # if object instantiation required
  159:     config:
  160:       test_empty: 1
  161:       test_nuls: 0
  162:       test_undef: 0
  163:       test_non_ascii: 0
  164: 
  165: =head2 Advanced Detection Capabilities
  166: 
  167: =over 4
  168: 
  169: =item * B<Accessor Method Detection>
  170: 
  171: Automatically identifies getter, setter, and combined accessor methods
  172: by analyzing common patterns like C<return $self-E<gt>{property}> and
  173: C<$self-E<gt>{property} = $value>.
  174: 
  175: =item * B<Params::Get Integration>
  176: 
  177: Recognises parameters extracted via C<Params::Get::get_params('key', \@_)>,
  178: treating the quoted key as a named parameter equivalent to a traditional
  179: C<my ($self, $key) = @_> signature.  This prevents false positives from
  180: C<--strict-pod> when the method body never declares an explicit C<$key>
  181: variable.
  182: 
  183: =item * B<Direct-Index Self Style>
  184: 
  185: Recognises C<my $self = $_[0]> as a valid method-invocant pattern.  Parameters
  186: at C<$_[1]>, C<$_[2]>, etc. are extracted as positional parameters.  Without
  187: this, the signature fallback would incorrectly pick up C<my (...) = @_> from
  188: inner closures defined in the method body and treat those variables as the
  189: outer method's parameters.
  190: 
  191: =item * B<Boolean Return Inference>
  192: 
  193: Detects boolean-returning methods through multiple signals:
  194:   - Method name patterns (is_*, has_*, can_*)
  195:   - Return patterns (consistent 1/0 returns)
  196:   - POD descriptions ("returns true on success")
  197:   - Ternary operators with boolean results
  198: 
  199: =item * B<Context Awareness>
  200: 
  201: Identifies methods that use C<wantarray> and can return different
  202: values in scalar vs list context.
  203: 
  204: =item * B<Object Lifecycle Management>
  205: 
  206: Detects instance methods requiring object instantiation and
  207: automatically adds the C<new> field to schemas.
  208: 
  209: =item * B<Enhanced Object Detection>
  210: 
  211: The extractor includes sophisticated object detection capabilities that go beyond simple instance method identification:
  212: 
  213: =over 4
  214: 
  215: =item * B<Factory Method Recognition>
  216: 
  217: Automatically identifies methods that create and return object instances, such as methods named C<create_*>, C<make_*>, C<build_*>, or C<get_*>. Factory methods are correctly classified as class methods that don't require pre-existing objects for testing.
  218: 
  219: =item * B<Singleton Pattern Detection>
  220: 
  221: Recognizes singleton patterns through multiple signals: method names like C<instance> or C<get_instance>, static variables holding instance references, lazy initialization patterns (C<$instance ||= new()>), and consistent return of the same instance variable.
  222: 
  223: =item * B<Constructor Parameter Analysis>
  224: 
  225: Examines C<new> methods to determine required and optional parameters, validation requirements, and default values. This enables test generators to provide appropriate constructor arguments when object instantiation is needed.
  226: 
  227: =item * B<Inheritance Relationship Handling>
  228: 
  229: Detects parent classes through C<use parent>, C<use base>, and C<@ISA> declarations. Identifies when methods use C<SUPER::> calls and determines whether the current class or a parent class constructor should be used for object instantiation.
  230: 
  231: =item * B<External Object Dependency Detection>
  232: 
  233: Identifies when methods create or depend on objects from other classes, enabling proper test setup with mock objects or real dependencies.
  234: 
  235: =back
  236: 
  237: These enhancements ensure that generated test schemas accurately reflect the object-oriented structure of the code, leading to more meaningful and effective test generation.
  238: 
  239: =back
  240: 
  241: =head2 Confidence Scoring
  242: 
  243: Each generated schema includes detailed confidence assessments:
  244: 
  245: =over 4
  246: 
  247: =item * B<High Confidence>
  248: 
  249: Multiple independent analysis sources converge on consistent,
  250: well-constrained parameters with explicit validation logic and
  251: comprehensive documentation.
  252: 
  253: =item * B<Medium Confidence>
  254: 
  255: Reasonable evidence from code patterns or partial documentation,
  256: but may lack comprehensive constraints or have some ambiguities.
  257: 
  258: =item * B<Low Confidence>
  259: 
  260: Minimal evidence - primarily based on naming conventions,
  261: default assumptions, or single-source analysis.
  262: 
  263: =item * B<Very Low Confidence>
  264: 
  265: Barely any detectable signals - schema should be thoroughly
  266: reviewed before use in test generation.
  267: 
  268: =back
  269: 
  270: =head2 Use Cases
  271: 
  272: =over 4
  273: 
  274: =item * B<Automated Test Generation>
  275: 
  276: Generate comprehensive test suites with L<App::Test::Generator> using
  277: extracted schemas as input. The schemas provide the necessary structure
  278: for generating both positive and negative test cases.
  279: 
  280: =item * B<API Documentation Generation>
  281: 
  282: Supplement existing documentation with automatically inferred interface
  283: specifications, parameter requirements, and return types.
  284: 
  285: =item * B<Code Quality Assessment>
  286: 
  287: Identify methods with poor documentation, inconsistent parameter handling,
  288: or unclear interfaces that may benefit from refactoring.
  289: 
  290: =item * B<Refactoring Assistance>
  291: 
  292: Detect method dependencies, object instantiation requirements, and
  293: parameter usage patterns to inform refactoring decisions.
  294: 
  295: =item * B<Legacy Code Analysis>
  296: 
  297: Quickly understand the interface contracts of legacy Perl codebases
  298: without extensive manual code reading.
  299: 
  300: =back
  301: 
  302: =head2 Integration with Testing Ecosystem
  303: 
  304: The generated schemas are specifically designed to work with the
  305: L<App::Test::Generator> ecosystem:
  306: 
  307:     # Extract schemas from your module
  308:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(...);
  309:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
  310: 
  311:     # Use with test generator (typically as separate steps)
  312:     # fuzz-harness-generator -r schemas/method_name.yml
  313: 
  314: =head2 Limitations and Considerations
  315: 
  316: =over 4
  317: 
  318: =item * B<Dynamic Code Patterns>
  319: 
  320: Highly dynamic code (string evals, AUTOLOAD, symbolic references)
  321: may not be fully detected by static analysis.
  322: 
  323: =item * B<Complex Validation Logic>
  324: 
  325: Sophisticated validation involving multiple parameters or external
  326: dependencies may require manual schema refinement.
  327: 
  328: =item * B<Confidence Heuristics>
  329: 
  330: Confidence scores are based on heuristics and should be reviewed
  331: by developers familiar with the codebase.
  332: 
  333: =item * B<Perl Idiom Recognition>
  334: 
  335: Some Perl-specific idioms may require custom pattern recognition
  336: beyond the built-in detectors.
  337: 
  338: =item * B<Documentation Dependency>
  339: 
  340: Analysis quality improves significantly with comprehensive POD
  341: documentation following consistent patterns.
  342: 
  343: =back
  344: 
  345: =head2 Best Practices for Optimal Results
  346: 
  347: =over 4
  348: 
  349: =item * B<Comprehensive POD Documentation>
  350: 
  351: Write detailed POD with explicit parameter documentation using
  352: consistent patterns like C<$param - type (constraints), description>.
  353: 
  354: =item * B<Consistent Coding Patterns>
  355: 
  356: Use consistent parameter validation patterns and method signatures
  357: throughout your codebase.
  358: 
  359: =item * B<Schema Review Process>
  360: 
  361: Review and refine automatically generated schemas, particularly
  362: those with low confidence scores.
  363: 
  364: =item * B<Descriptive Naming>
  365: 
  366: Use descriptive method and parameter names that clearly indicate
  367: purpose and expected types.
  368: 
  369: =item * B<Progressive Enhancement>
  370: 
  371: Start with automatically generated schemas and progressively
  372: refine them based on test results and code understanding.
  373: 
  374: =back
  375: 
  376: The module is particularly valuable for large codebases where manual schema
  377: creation would be prohibitively time-consuming, and for maintaining test
  378: coverage as code evolves through continuous integration pipelines.
  379: 
  380: =head2 Advanced Type Detection
  381: 
  382: The schema extractor includes enhanced type detection capabilities that identify specialized Perl types beyond basic strings and integers.
  383: L<DateTime> and L<Time::Piece> objects are detected through isa() checks and method call patterns, while date strings (ISO 8601, YYYY-MM-DD) and UNIX timestamps are recognized through regex validation and numeric range checks.
  384: File handles and file paths are identified via I/O operations and file test operators, coderefs are detected through ref() checks and invocation patterns, and enum-like parameters are extracted from validation code including regex patterns (C</^(a|b|c)$/>), hash lookups, grep statements, and if/elsif chains.
  385: These detected types are preserved in the generated YAML schemas with appropriate semantic annotations, enabling test generators to create more accurate and meaningful test cases.
  386: 
  387: =head3 Example Advanced Type Schema
  388: 
  389: For a method like:
  390: 
  391:     sub process_event {
  392:         my ($self, $timestamp, $status, $callback) = @_;
  393:         croak unless $timestamp > 1000000000;
  394:         croak unless $status =~ /^(active|pending|complete)$/;
  395:         croak unless ref($callback) eq 'CODE';
  396:         $callback->($timestamp, $status);
  397:     }
  398: 
  399: The extractor generates:
  400: 
  401:     ---
  402:     function: process_event
  403:     module: MyModule
  404:     input:
  405:       timestamp:
  406:         type: integer
  407:         # min: 0
  408:         # max: 2147483647
  409:         position: 0
  410:         _note: Unix timestamp
  411: 	semantic: unix_timestamp
  412:       status:
  413:         type: string
  414:         enum:
  415:           - active
  416:           - pending
  417:           - complete
  418:         position: 1
  419:         _note: 'Must be one of: active, pending, complete'
  420:       callback:
  421:         type: coderef
  422:         position: 2
  423:         _note: 'CODE reference - provide sub { } in tests'
  424: 
  425: =head1 RELATIONSHIP DETECTION
  426: 
  427: The schema extractor detects relationships and dependencies between parameters,
  428: enabling more sophisticated validation and test generation.
  429: 
  430: =head2 Relationship Types
  431: 
  432: =over 4
  433: 
  434: =item * B<mutually_exclusive>
  435: 
  436: Parameters that cannot be used together.
  437: 
  438:     die if $file && $content;  # Can't specify both
  439: 
  440: Generated schema:
  441: 
  442:     relationships:
  443:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  444:         params: [file, content]
  445:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  446: 
  447: =item * B<required_group>
  448: 
  449: At least one parameter from the group must be specified (OR logic).
  450: 
  451:     die unless $id || $name;  # Must provide one
  452: 
  453: Generated schema:
  454: 
  455:     relationships:
  456:       - type: required_group
  457:         params: [id, name]
  458:         logic: or
  459:         description: Must specify either id or name
  460: 
  461: =item * B<conditional_requirement>
  462: 
  463: If one parameter is specified, another becomes required (IF-THEN logic).
  464: 
  465:     die if $async && !$callback;  # async requires callback
  466: 
  467: Generated schema:
  468: 
  469:     relationships:
  470:       - type: conditional_requirement
  471:         if: async
  472:         then_required: callback
  473:         description: When async is specified, callback is required
  474: 
  475: =item * B<dependency>
  476: 
  477: One parameter depends on another being present.
  478: 
  479:     die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host;
  480: 
  481: Generated schema:
  482: 
  483:     relationships:
  484:       - type: dependency
  485:         param: port
  486:         requires: host
  487:         description: port requires host to be specified
  488: 
  489: =item * B<value_constraint>
  490: 
  491: Specific value requirements between parameters.
  492: 
  493:     die if $ssl && $port != 443;  # ssl requires port 443
  494: 
  495: Generated schema:
  496: 
  497:     relationships:
  498:       - type: value_constraint
  499:         if: ssl
  500:         then: port
  501:         operator: ==
  502:         value: 443
  503:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  504: 
  505: =item * B<value_conditional>
  506: 
  507: Parameter required when another has a specific value.
  508: 
  509:     die if $mode eq 'secure' && !$key;
  510: 
  511: Generated schema:
  512: 
  513:     relationships:
  514:       - type: value_conditional
  515:         if: mode
  516:         equals: secure
  517:         then_required: key
  518:         description: When mode equals 'secure', key is required
  519: 
  520: =back
  521: 
  522: =head2 Default Value Extraction
  523: 
  524: The extractor comprehensively extracts default values from both code and POD documentation:
  525: 
  526: =head3 Code Pattern Recognition
  527: 
  528: Extracts defaults from multiple Perl idioms:
  529: 
  530: =over 4
  531: 
  532: =item * Logical OR operator: C<$param = $param || 'default'>
  533: 
  534: =item * Defined-or operator: C<$param //= 'default'>
  535: 
  536: =item * Ternary operator: C<$param = defined $param ? $param : 'default'>
  537: 
  538: =item * Unless conditional: C<$param = 'default' unless defined $param>
  539: 
  540: =item * Chained defaults: C<$param = $param || $self->{_default} || 'fallback'>
  541: 
  542: =item * Multi-line patterns: C<$param = {} unless $param>
  543: 
  544: =back
  545: 
  546: =head3 POD Pattern Recognition
  547: 
  548: Extracts defaults from documentation:
  549: 
  550: =over 4
  551: 
  552: =item * Standard format: C<Default: 'value'>
  553: 
  554: =item * Alternative format: C<Defaults to: 'value'>
  555: 
  556: =item * Inline format: C<Optional, default: 'value'>
  557: 
  558: =item * Parameter lists: C<$param - type, default 'value'>
  559: 
  560: =back
  561: 
  562: =head3 Value Processing
  563: 
  564: Properly handles:
  565: 
  566: =over 4
  567: 
  568: =item * String literals with quotes and escape sequences
  569: 
  570: =item * Numeric values (integers and floats)
  571: 
  572: =item * Boolean values (true/false converted to 1/0)
  573: 
  574: =item * Empty data structures ([] and {})
  575: 
  576: =item * Special values (undef, __PACKAGE__)
  577: 
  578: =item * Complex expressions (preserved as-is when unevaluatable)
  579: 
  580: =item * Quote operators (q{}, qq{}, qw{})
  581: 
  582: =back
  583: 
  584: =head3 Type Inference
  585: 
  586: When a parameter has a default value but no explicit type annotation,
  587: the type is automatically inferred from the default:
  588: 
  589:     $options = {}        # inferred as hashref
  590:     $items = []          # inferred as arrayref
  591:     $count = 42          # inferred as integer
  592:     $ratio = 3.14        # inferred as number
  593:     $enabled = 1         # inferred as boolean
  594: 
  595: =head2 Context-Aware Return Analysis
  596: 
  597: The extractor provides comprehensive analysis of method return behavior,
  598: including context sensitivity, error handling conventions, and method chaining patterns.
  599: 
  600: When a method's POD contains a C<=head4 Output> block in
  601: L<Params::Validate::Strict> schema format, the C<type> declared there is
  602: used as the authoritative output type and takes precedence over all
  603: heuristic code analysis:
  604: 
  605:     =head4 Output
  606: 
  607:         {
  608:             type => 'hashref',
  609:         }
  610: 
  611: This is the recommended way to document methods whose return type would
  612: otherwise be misidentified (e.g. a method that returns C<$self-E<gt>{cache}>
  613: where the cache happens to hold a hashref).
  614: 
  615: =head3 List vs Scalar Context Detection
  616: 
  617: Automatically detects methods that return different values based on calling context:
  618: 
  619:     sub get_items {
  620:         my $self = $_[0];
  621:         return wantarray ? @items : scalar(@items);
  622:     }
  623: 
  624: Detection captures:
  625: 
  626: =over 4
  627: 
  628: =item * C<_context_aware> flag - Method uses wantarray
  629: 
  630: =item * C<_list_context> - Type returned in list context (e.g., 'array')
  631: 
  632: =item * C<_scalar_context> - Type returned in scalar context (e.g., 'integer')
  633: 
  634: =back
  635: 
  636: Recognizes both ternary operator patterns and conditional return patterns.
  637: 
  638: =head3 Void Context Methods
  639: 
  640: Identifies methods that don't return meaningful values:
  641: 
  642: =over 4
  643: 
  644: =item * Setters (C<set_*> methods)
  645: 
  646: =item * Mutators (C<add_*, remove_*, delete_*, clear_*, reset_*, update_*>)
  647: 
  648: =item * Loggers (C<log, debug, warn, error, info>)
  649: 
  650: =item * Methods with only empty returns
  651: 
  652: =back
  653: 
  654: Example:
  655: 
  656:     sub set_name {
  657:         my ($self, $name) = @_;
  658:         $self->{name} = $name;
  659:         return;  # Void context
  660:     }
  661: 
  662: Sets C<_void_context> flag and C<type =E<gt> 'void'>.
  663: 
  664: =head3 Method Chaining Detection
  665: 
  666: Identifies chainable methods that return C<$self> for fluent interfaces:
  667: 
  668:     sub set_width {
  669:         my ($self, $width) = @_;
  670:         $self->{width} = $width;
  671:         return $self;  # Chainable
  672:     }
  673: 
  674: Detection provides:
  675: 
  676: =over 4
  677: 
  678: =item * C<_returns_self> - Returns invocant for chaining
  679: 
  680: =item * C<class> - The class name being returned
  681: 
  682: =back
  683: 
  684: Also detects chaining documentation in POD (keywords: "chainable", "fluent interface",
  685: "returns self", "method chaining").
  686: 
  687: =head3 Error Return Conventions
  688: 
  689: Analyzes how methods signal errors:
  690: 
  691: B<Pattern Detection:>
  692: 
  693: =over 4
  694: 
  695: =item * C<undef_on_error> - Explicit C<return undef if/unless condition>
  696: 
  697: =item * C<implicit_undef> - Bare C<return if/unless condition>
  698: 
  699: =item * C<empty_list> - C<return ()> for list context errors
  700: 
  701: =item * C<zero_on_error> - Returns 0/false for boolean error indication
  702: 
  703: =item * C<exception_handling> - Uses eval blocks with error checking
  704: 
  705: =back
  706: 
  707: B<Example Analysis:>
  708: 
  709:     sub fetch_user {
  710:         my ($self, $id) = @_;
  711: 
  712:         return undef unless $id;        # undef_on_error
  713:         return undef if $id < 0;        # undef_on_error
  714: 
  715:         return $self->{users}{$id};
  716:     }
  717: 
  718: Results in:
  719: 
  720:     _error_return: 'undef'
  721:     _success_failure_pattern: 1
  722:     _error_handling: {
  723:         undef_on_error: ['$id', '$id < 0']
  724:     }
  725: 
  726: B<Success/Failure Pattern:>
  727: 
  728: Methods that return different types for success vs. failure are flagged with
  729: C<_success_failure_pattern>. Common patterns:
  730: 
  731: =over 4
  732: 
  733: =item * Returns value on success, undef on failure
  734: 
  735: =item * Returns true on success, false on failure
  736: 
  737: =item * Returns data on success, empty list on failure
  738: 
  739: =back
  740: 
  741: =head3 Success Indicator Detection
  742: 
  743: Methods that always return true (typically for side effects):
  744: 
  745:     sub update_status {
  746:         my ($self, $status) = @_;
  747:         $self->{status} = $status;
  748:         return 1;  # Success indicator
  749:     }
  750: 
  751: Sets C<_success_indicator> flag when method consistently returns 1.
  752: 
  753: =head3 Schema Output
  754: 
  755: Enhanced return analysis adds these fields to method schemas:
  756: 
  757:     output:
  758:       type: boolean              # Inferred return type
  759:       _context_aware: 1           # Uses wantarray
  760:       _list_context:
  761:         type: array
  762:       _scalar_context:
  763:         type: integer
  764:       _returns_self: 1               # Returns $self
  765:       _void_context: 1            # No meaningful return
  766:       _success_indicator: 1       # Always returns true
  767:       _error_return: undef        # How errors are signaled
  768:       _success_failure_pattern: 1 # Mixed return types
  769:       _error_handling:            # Detailed error patterns
  770:         undef_on_error: [...]
  771:         exception_handling: 1
  772: 
  773: This comprehensive analysis enables:
  774: 
  775: =over 4
  776: 
  777: =item * Better test generation (testing both contexts, error paths)
  778: 
  779: =item * Documentation generation (clear error conventions)
  780: 
  781: =item * API design validation (consistent error handling)
  782: 
  783: =item * Contract specification (precise return behavior)
  784: 
  785: =back
  786: 
  787: =head2 Example
  788: 
  789: For a method like:
  790: 
  791:     sub connect {
  792:         my ($self, $host, $port, $ssl, $file, $content) = @_;
  793: 
  794:         die if $file && $content;                    # mutually exclusive
  795:         die unless $host || $file;                   # required group
  796:         die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host; # dependency
  797:         die if $ssl && $port != 443;                 # value constraint
  798: 
  799:         # ... connection logic
  800:     }
  801: 
  802: The extractor generates:
  803: 
  804:     relationships:
  805:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  806:         params: [file, content]
  807:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  808:       - type: required_group
  809:         params: [host, file]
  810:         logic: or
  811:         description: Must specify either host or file
  812:       - type: dependency
  813:         param: port
  814:         requires: host
  815:         description: port requires host to be specified
  816:       - type: value_constraint
  817:         if: ssl
  818:         then: port
  819:         operator: ==
  820:         value: 443
  821:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  822: 
  823: =head1 MODERN PERL FEATURES
  824: 
  825: This module adds support for:
  826: 
  827: =head2 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  828: 
  829:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, %options) {
  830:         ...
  831:     }
  832: 
  833: Extracts: required params, optional params with defaults, slurpy params
  834: 
  835: =head2 Type Constraints (Perl 5.36+)
  836: 
  837:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num) {
  838:         ...
  839:     }
  840: 
  841: Recognizes: Int, Num, Str, Bool, ArrayRef, HashRef, custom classes
  842: 
  843: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  844: 
  845:     sub get_value :lvalue :Returns(Int) {
  846:         ...
  847:     }
  848: 
  849: Detects: :lvalue, :method, :Returns(Type), custom attributes
  850: 
  851: =head2 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  852: 
  853:     my @array = $arrayref->@*;
  854:     my %hash = $hashref->%*;
  855:     my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];
  856: 
  857: Tracks usage of modern dereferencing syntax
  858: 
  859: =head2 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
  860: 
  861:     field $host :param = 'localhost';
  862:     field $port :param(port_number) = 3306;
  863:     field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
  864: 
  865: Extracts fields and maps them to parameters
  866: 
  867: =head2 Modern Perl Features Support
  868: 
  869: The schema extractor supports modern Perl syntax introduced in versions 5.20, 5.36, and 5.38+.
  870: 
  871: =head3 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  872: 
  873: Automatically extracts parameters from native Perl signatures:
  874: 
  875:     use feature 'signatures';
  876: 
  877:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, $database = undef) {
  878:         ...
  879:     }
  880: 
  881: Extracted schema includes:
  882: 
  883: =over 4
  884: 
  885: =item * Parameter positions
  886: 
  887: =item * Optional vs required parameters
  888: 
  889: =item * Default values from signature
  890: 
  891: =item * Slurpy parameters (@array, %hash)
  892: 
  893: =back
  894: 
  895: B<Example:>
  896: 
  897:     # Signature with defaults
  898:     sub process($file, %options) { ... }
  899: 
  900:     # Extracts:
  901:     # $file: position 0, required
  902:     # %options: position 1, optional, slurpy hash
  903: 
  904: =head3 Type Constraints in Signatures (Perl 5.36+)
  905: 
  906: Recognizes type constraints in signature parameters:
  907: 
  908:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num, $name :Str = "result") {
  909:         return $x + $y;
  910:     }
  911: 
  912: Supported constraint types:
  913: 
  914: =over 4
  915: 
  916: =item * C<:Int, :Integer> -> integer
  917: 
  918: =item * C<:Num, :Number> -> number
  919: 
  920: =item * C<:Str, :String> -> string
  921: 
  922: =item * C<:Bool, :Boolean> -> boolean
  923: 
  924: =item * C<:ArrayRef, :Array> -> arrayref
  925: 
  926: =item * C<:HashRef, :Hash> -> hashref
  927: 
  928: =item * C<:ClassName> -> object with isa constraint
  929: 
  930: =back
  931: 
  932: Type constraints are combined with defaults when both are present.
  933: 
  934: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  935: 
  936: Extracts and documents subroutine attributes:
  937: 
  938:     sub get_value :lvalue {
  939:         my $self = shift;
  940:         return $self->{value};
  941:     }
  942: 
  943:     sub calculate :Returns(Int) :method {
  944:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
  945:         return $x + $y;
  946:     }
  947: 
  948: Recognized attributes stored in C<_attributes> field:
  949: 
  950: =over 4
  951: 
  952: =item * C<:lvalue> - Method can be assigned to
  953: 
  954: =item * C<:method> - Explicitly marked as method
  955: 
  956: =item * C<:Returns(Type)> - Declares return type
  957: 
  958: =item * Custom attributes with values: C<:MyAttr(value)>
  959: 
  960: =back
  961: 
  962: =head3 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  963: 
  964: Detects usage of postfix dereferencing syntax:
  965: 
  966:     use feature 'postderef';
  967: 
  968:     sub process_array {
  969:         my ($self, $arrayref) = @_;
  970:         my @array = $arrayref->@*;        # Array dereference
  971:         my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];  # Array slice
  972:         return @array;
  973:     }
  974: 
  975:     sub process_hash {
  976:         my ($self, $hashref) = @_;
  977:         my %hash = $hashref->%*;          # Hash dereference
  978:         return keys %hash;
  979:     }
  980: 
  981: Tracked features stored in C<_modern_features>:
  982: 
  983: =over 4
  984: 
  985: =item * C<array_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>@*>
  986: 
  987: =item * C<hash_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>%*>
  988: 
  989: =item * C<scalar_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>$*>
  990: 
  991: =item * C<code_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>&*>
  992: 
  993: =item * C<array_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>@[...]>
  994: 
  995: =item * C<hash_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>%{...}>
  996: 
  997: =back
  998: 
  999: =head3 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
 1000: 
 1001: Extracts field declarations from class syntax and maps them to method parameters:
 1002: 
 1003:     use feature 'class';
 1004: 
 1005:     class DatabaseConnection {
 1006:         field $host :param = 'localhost';
 1007:         field $port :param = 3306;
 1008:         field $username :param(user);
 1009:         field $password :param;
 1010:         field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
 1011: 
 1012:         method connect() {
 1013:             # Fields available as instance variables
 1014:         }
 1015:     }
 1016: 
 1017: Field attributes:
 1018: 
 1019: =over 4
 1020: 
 1021: =item * C<:param> - Field is a constructor parameter (uses field name)
 1022: 
 1023: =item * C<:param(name)> - Field maps to parameter with different name
 1024: 
 1025: =item * C<:isa(Class)> - Type constraint for the field
 1026: 
 1027: =item * Default values in field declarations
 1028: 
 1029: =back
 1030: 
 1031: Extracted schema includes both field information in C<_fields> and merged parameter
 1032: information in C<input>, allowing proper validation of class constructors.
 1033: 
 1034: =head3 Mixed Modern and Traditional Syntax
 1035: 
 1036: The extractor handles code that mixes modern and traditional syntax:
 1037: 
 1038:     sub modern($x, $y = 5) {
 1039:         # Modern signature with default
 1040:     }
 1041: 
 1042:     sub traditional {
 1043:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
 1044:         $y //= 5;  # Traditional default in code
 1045:         # Both extract same parameter information
 1046:     }
 1047: 
 1048: Priority order for parameter information:
 1049: 
 1050: =over 4
 1051: 
 1052: =item 1. Signature declarations (highest priority)
 1053: 
 1054: =item 2. Field declarations (for class methods)
 1055: 
 1056: =item 3. POD documentation
 1057: 
 1058: =item 4. Code analysis (lowest priority)
 1059: 
 1060: =back
 1061: 
 1062: This ensures that explicit declarations in signatures take precedence over
 1063: inferred information from code analysis.
 1064: 
 1065: =head3 Backwards Compatibility
 1066: 
 1067: All modern Perl feature detection is optional and automatic:
 1068: 
 1069: =over 4
 1070: 
 1071: =item * Traditional C<sub> declarations continue to work
 1072: 
 1073: =item * Code without modern features extracts parameters as before
 1074: 
 1075: =item * Modern features are additive - they enhance rather than replace existing extraction
 1076: 
 1077: =item * Schemas include C<_source> field indicating where parameter info came from
 1078: 
 1079: =back
 1080: 
 1081: =head2 _yamltest_hints
 1082: 
 1083: Each method schema returned by L</extract_all> now optionally includes a
 1084: C<_yamltest_hints> key, which provides guidance for automated test generation
 1085: based on the code analysis.
 1086: 
 1087: This is intended to help L<App::Test::Generator> create meaningful tests,
 1088: including boundary and invalid input cases, without manually specifying them.
 1089: 
 1090: The structure is a hashref with the following keys:
 1091: 
 1092: =over 4
 1093: 
 1094: =item * boundary_values
 1095: 
 1096: An arrayref of numeric values that represent boundaries detected from
 1097: comparisons in the code. These are derived from literals in statements
 1098: like C<$x < 0> or C<$y >= 255>. The generator can use these to create
 1099: boundary tests.
 1100: 
 1101: Example:
 1102: 
 1103:     _yamltest_hints:
 1104:       boundary_values: [0, 1, 100, 255]
 1105: 
 1106: =item * invalid_inputs
 1107: 
 1108: An arrayref of values that are likely to be rejected by the method,
 1109: based on checks like C<defined>, empty strings, or numeric validations.
 1110: 
 1111: Example:
 1112: 
 1113:     _yamltest_hints:
 1114:       invalid_inputs: [undef, '', -1]
 1115: 
 1116: =item * equivalence_classes
 1117: 
 1118: An arrayref intended to capture detected equivalence classes or patterns
 1119: among inputs. Currently this is empty by default, but future enhancements
 1120: may populate it based on detected input groupings.
 1121: 
 1122: Example:
 1123: 
 1124:     _yamltest_hints:
 1125:       equivalence_classes: []
 1126: 
 1127: =back
 1128: 
 1129: =head3 Usage
 1130: 
 1131: When calling C<extract_all>, each method schema will include
 1132: C<_yamltest_hints> if any hints were detected:
 1133: 
 1134:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1135:     my $hints  = $schemas->{example_method}->{_yamltest_hints};
 1136: 
 1137: You can then feed these hints into automated test generators to produce
 1138: negative tests, boundary tests, and parameter-specific test cases.
 1139: 
 1140: =head3 Notes
 1141: 
 1142: =over 4
 1143: 
 1144: =item * Hints are inferred heuristically from code and validation statements.
 1145: 
 1146: =item * Not all inputs are guaranteed to be detected; the feature is additive
 1147: and will never remove information from the schema.
 1148: 
 1149: =item * Currently, equivalence classes are not populated, but the field exists
 1150: for future extension.
 1151: 
 1152: =item * Boundary and invalid input hints are deduplicated to avoid repeated
 1153: test values.
 1154: 
 1155: =back
 1156: 
 1157: =head3 Examples
 1158: 
 1159: Given a method like:
 1160: 
 1161:     sub example {
 1162:         my ($x) = @_;
 1163:         die "negative" if $x < 0;
 1164:         return unless defined($x);
 1165:         return $x * 2;
 1166:     }
 1167: 
 1168: After running:
 1169: 
 1170:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1171:         input_file => 'TestHints.pm',
 1172:         output_dir => '/tmp',
 1173:         quiet    => 1,
 1174:     );
 1175: 
 1176:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1177: 
 1178: The schema for the method "example" will include:
 1179: 
 1180:     $schemas->{example} = {
 1181:         function => 'example',
 1182:         _confidence => {
 1183:             input  => 'unknown',
 1184:             output => 'unknown',
 1185:         },
 1186:         input => {
 1187:             x => {
 1188:                 type     => 'scalar',
 1189:                 optional => 0,
 1190:             }
 1191:         },
 1192:         output => {
 1193:             type => 'scalar',
 1194:         },
 1195:         _yamltest_hints => {
 1196:             boundary_values => [0, 1],
 1197:             invalid_inputs  => [undef, -1],
 1198:             equivalence_classes => [],
 1199:         },
 1200:         _notes => '...',
 1201:         _analysis => {
 1202:             input_confidence  => 'low',
 1203:             output_confidence => 'unknown',
 1204:             confidence_factors => {
 1205:                 input  => {...},
 1206:                 output => {...},
 1207:             },
 1208:             overall_confidence => 'low',
 1209:         },
 1210:         _fields => {},
 1211:         _modern_features => {},
 1212:         _attributes => {},
 1213:     };
 1214: 
 1215: =head1 METHODS
 1216: 
 1217: =head2 new
 1218: 
 1219: Construct a new SchemaExtractor for a given Perl source file.
 1220: 
 1221:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1222:         input_file           => 'lib/MyModule.pm',  # Required
 1223:         output_dir           => 'schemas/',         # Optional - only needed if writing schemas
 1224:         verbose              => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1225:         include_private      => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1226:         max_parameters       => 50,                 # Default: 20
 1227:         confidence_threshold => 0.7,               # Default: 0.5
 1228:         strict_pod           => 0|1|2,              # Default: 0 (off)
 1229:     );
 1230: 
 1231: =head3 Arguments
 1232: 
 1233: =over 4
 1234: 
 1235: =item * C<input_file>
 1236: 
 1237: Path to the Perl source file to analyse. Required. Must exist on disk.
 1238: 
 1239: =item * C<output_dir>
 1240: 
 1241: Directory to write generated schema YAML files. Optional - only
 1242: required if C<_write_schema> will be called. Callers passing
 1243: C<no_write =E<gt> 1> to C<extract_all> do not need to supply it.
 1244: 
 1245: =item * C<verbose>
 1246: 
 1247: Print progress messages to stdout during analysis. Optional, default 0.
 1248: 
 1249: =item * C<include_private>
 1250: 
 1251: Include methods whose names begin with C<_> in the analysis. Optional,
 1252: default 0. Methods named C<_new>, C<_init>, and C<_build> are always
 1253: included regardless of this setting.
 1254: 
 1255: =item * C<max_parameters>
 1256: 
 1257: Safety limit on the number of parameters analysed per method to prevent
 1258: runaway processing on pathological code. Optional, default 20.
 1259: 
 1260: =item * C<confidence_threshold>
 1261: 
 1262: Minimum confidence score (0.0-1.0) below which a schema is marked with
 1263: C<_low_confidence =E<gt> 1>. Optional, default 0.5.
 1264: 
 1265: =item * C<strict_pod>
 1266: 
 1267: Controls POD/code agreement validation. C<0> disables validation,
 1268: C<1> emits warnings, C<2> croaks on first disagreement. Also accepts
 1269: the strings C<off>, C<warn>, and C<fatal>. Optional, default 0.
 1270: 
 1271: =back
 1272: 
 1273: =head3 Returns
 1274: 
 1275: A blessed hashref. Croaks if C<input_file> is missing or does not
 1276: exist on disk.
 1277: 
 1278: =head3 Side effects
 1279: 
 1280: Reads and parses the input file using L<PPI> at construction time.
 1281: 
 1282: =head3 API specification
 1283: 
 1284: =head4 input
 1285: 
 1286:     {
 1287:         input_file           => { type => SCALAR },
 1288:         output_dir           => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1289:         verbose              => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1290:         include_private      => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1291:         max_parameters       => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1292:         confidence_threshold => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1293:         strict_pod           => { type => SCALAR,  optional => 1 },
 1294:     }
 1295: 
 1296: =head4 output
 1297: 
 1298:     {
 1299:         type => OBJECT,
 1300:         isa  => 'App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor',
 1301:     }
 1302: 
 1303: =cut
 1304: 
 1305: sub new {

 1332: 
 1333: =head2 extract_all
 1334: 
 1335: Extract schemas for all qualifying methods in the module and return
 1336: them as a hashref.
 1337: 
 1338:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
 1339: 
 1340:     # Suppress writing .yml files to disk
 1341:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all(no_write => 1);
 1342: 
 1343: =head3 Arguments
 1344: 
 1345: =over 4
 1346: 
 1347: =item * C<no_write>
 1348: 
 1349: When true, schema files are not written to C<output_dir>. The returned
 1350: hashref is still fully populated. Useful when the caller wants to
 1351: inspect or augment schemas before deciding whether to write them.
 1352: Optional, default 0.
 1353: 
 1354: =back
 1355: 
 1356: =head3 Returns
 1357: 
 1358: A hashref mapping method name strings to schema hashrefs. Each schema
 1359: contains at minimum the keys C<function>, C<module>, C<input>,
 1360: C<output>, and C<_analysis>. See L</Generated Schema Structure> for
 1361: the full structure.
 1362: 
 1363: =head3 Side effects
 1364: 
 1365: Parses the input file with L<PPI>. Writes one YAML file per method to
 1366: C<output_dir> unless C<no_write> is set. Creates C<output_dir> if it
 1367: does not exist and writing is enabled.
 1368: 
 1369: =head3 Notes
 1370: 
 1371: Private methods (names beginning with C<_>) are excluded unless
 1372: C<include_private =E<gt> 1> was passed to C<new>. Duplicate method
 1373: names are deduplicated with a warning logged to stdout in verbose mode.
 1374: 
 1375: POD/code agreement validation is applied if C<strict_pod> was set in
 1376: C<new>. At level 2 (fatal), the first disagreement causes an immediate
 1377: croak.
 1378: 
 1379: =head3 API specification
 1380: 
 1381: =head4 input
 1382: 
 1383:     {
 1384:         self     => { type => OBJECT, isa => 'App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor' },
 1385:         no_write => { type => SCALAR, optional => 1 },
 1386:     }
 1387: 
 1388: =head4 output
 1389: 
 1390:     {
 1391:         type => HASHREF,
 1392:         keys => {
 1393:             '*' => {

 3588: #             return value by combining POD return

 3599: #                            boolean heuristics.
 3600: #
 3601: # Exit:       Returns a hashref describing the
 3602: #             output type and behaviour, or an empty
 3603: #             hashref if nothing could be determined.
 3604: #             Keys include: type, value, isa, and
 3605: #             various _* metadata keys.
 3606: #
 3607: # Side effects: Logs progress to stdout when
 3608: #               verbose is set.
 3609: # --------------------------------------------------
 3610: sub _analyze_output {
 3611: 	my ($self, $pod, $code, $method_name) = @_;
 3612: 
 3613: 	my %output;
 3614: 
 3615: 	$self->_analyze_output_from_pod(\%output, $pod);
 3616: 	$self->_analyze_output_from_code(\%output, $code, $method_name);
 3617: 	$self->_enhance_boolean_detection(\%output, $pod, $code, $method_name);
 3618: 	$self->_detect_list_context(\%output, $code);
 3619: 	$self->_detect_void_context(\%output, $code, $method_name);
 3620: 	$self->_detect_chaining_pattern(\%output, $code);
 3621: 	$self->_detect_error_conventions(\%output, $code);
 3622: 
 3623: 	$self->_validate_output(\%output) if keys %output;
 3624: 
 3625: 	# Don't return empty output
 3626: 	return (keys %output) ? \%output : {};
 3627: }

 5029: # --------------------------------------------------
 5030: # _analyze_advanced_types
 5031: #
 5032: # Purpose:    Apply enhanced type detection to a
 5033: #             single parameter, checking for
 5034: #             DateTime objects, file handles,
 5035: #             coderefs, and enum-like constraints
 5036: #             beyond what basic type inference
 5037: #             can determine.
 5038: #
 5039: # Entry:      $p_ref - reference to the parameter
 5040: #                      hashref (modified in place
 5041: #                      via the referenced hash).
 5042: #             $param - the parameter name string.
 5043: #             $code  - method body source string.
 5044: #
 5045: # Exit:       Returns nothing. Modifies the
 5046: #             referenced parameter hashref in place.
 5047: #
 5048: # Side effects: Logs detections to stdout when
 5049: #               verbose is set.
 5050: #
 5051: # Notes:      Delegates to four specialised
 5052: #             detectors: _detect_datetime_type,
 5053: #             _detect_filehandle_type,
 5054: #             _detect_coderef_type, and
 5055: #             _detect_enum_type. Each detector
 5056: #             returns early on first match so
 5057: #             detectors are implicitly prioritised
 5058: #             in that order.
 5059: # --------------------------------------------------
 5060: sub _analyze_advanced_types {
 5061: 	my ($self, $p_ref, $param, $code) = @_;
 5062: 
 5063: 	# Dereference once to get the hash reference
 5064: 	my $p = $$p_ref;
 5065: 
 5066: 	# Now pass the dereferenced hash to the detection methods
 5067: 	$self->_detect_datetime_type($p, $param, $code);
 5068: 	$self->_detect_filehandle_type($p, $param, $code);
 5069: 	$self->_detect_coderef_type($p, $param, $code);
 5070: 	$self->_detect_enum_type($p, $param, $code);
 5071: }

 9419: 
 9420: =head2 generate_pod_validation_report
 9421: 
 9422: Generate a human-readable report of all POD/code disagreements found
 9423: across a set of extracted schemas.
 9424: 
 9425:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all(no_write => 1);
 9426:     my $report  = $extractor->generate_pod_validation_report($schemas);
 9427:     print $report;
 9428: 
 9429: =head3 Arguments
 9430: 
 9431: =over 4
 9432: 
 9433: =item * C<$schemas>
 9434: 
 9435: A hashref of method name to schema hashref as returned by
 9436: C<extract_all>. Required.
 9437: 
 9438: =back
 9439: 
 9440: =head3 Returns
 9441: 
 9442: A string containing the full validation report, or a single line
 9443: confirming all methods passed if no disagreements were found.
 9444: 
 9445: =head3 Side effects
 9446: 
 9447: None.
 9448: 
 9449: =head3 Notes
 9450: 
 9451: Only methods whose schemas contain a C<_pod_validation_errors> key
 9452: (populated when C<strict_pod> is 1 or 2) appear in the report. If
 9453: C<strict_pod> was 0 when C<extract_all> was called, this method will
 9454: always return the all-passed message.
 9455: 
 9456: =head3 API specification
 9457: 
 9458: =head4 input
 9459: 
 9460:     {
 9461:         self    => { type => OBJECT,  isa => 'App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor' },
 9462:         schemas => { type => HASHREF },
 9463:     }
 9464: 
 9465: =head4 output
 9466: 
 9467:     { type => SCALAR }
 9468: 
 9469: =cut
 9470:

 9494: =head2 _log
 9495: 
 9496: Log a message if verbose mode is on.
 9497: 
 9498: =cut
 9499: 
 9500: sub _log {

 9506: =head1 NOTES
 9507: 
 9508: This is pre-pre-alpha proof of concept code.
 9509: Nevertheless,
 9510: it is useful for creating a template which you can modify to create a working schema to pass into L<App::Test::Generator>.
 9511: 
 9512: =head1 TODO
 9513: 
 9514: Extend C<=head4 Input> parsing to cover union types (e.g. C<scalar | scalarref>)
 9515: and the C<enum>/C<memberof> constraint synonym.
 9516: 
 9517: =head1 SEE ALSO
 9518: 
 9519: =over 4
 9520: 
 9521: =item * L<App::Test::Generator> - Generate fuzz and corpus-driven test harnesses
 9522: 
 9523: Output from this module serves as input to that module.
 9524: So with well-documented code, you can automatically create your tests.
 9525: 
 9526: =item * L<App::Test::Generator::Template> - Template of the file of tests created by C<App::Test::Generator>
 9527:
